Error: Cannot open the page from the filesystem.
  • Chrome: Install SingleFileZ and enable the option "Allow access to file URLs" in the details page of the extension (chrome://extensions/?id=offkdfbbigofcgdokjemgjpdockaafjg).
  • Microsoft Edge: Install SingleFileZ and enable the option "Allow access to file URLs" in the details page of the extension (edge://extensions/?id=gofneaifncimeglaecpnanbnmnpfjekk).
  • Safari: Select "Disable Local File Restrictions" in the "Develop" menu.

Last edited by verynice (2017-08-31 11:20:13) Offline #2 2017-08-22 15:08:06 Lone_Wolf Member From: Netherlands, Europe Registered: 2005-10-04 Posts: 10,766 Re: kernel crashing with radeon/amdgpu the kernel modules radeon and amdgpu function on a different level then the xf86-video-* packages.First step is to figure out if the problem is with starting X or earlier in start process .Remove radeon[1]  from the blacklist and configure your system to boot into multi-user mode.reboot, post full dmesg / journalctl output[1]your card can use either radeon kernel module or amdgpu module, but the radeon kernel module tends to be more reliable then amdgpu module. I manually went to the last reboot mark and delted the rest.man journalctl will help with that, look up the -b  / --boot option.The log looks good, and i assume you see a normal console screen ?login as user, create a ~/xinitrc and remove any xorg configuration files.run startx , post X log .------------------------------------------The linux graphics stack is kinda complicated, see http://blog.mecheye.net/2012/06/the-lin … ics-stack/ .Short version : If the linux graphics stack was a skycraper, xf86 packages would live in the penthouse and the kernel modules in the basement. I still start xorg manually with startx.I already created an xinitrc file and it looks like this:#!/bin/sh userresources=$HOME/.Xresources usermodmap=$HOME/.Xmodmap sysresources=/etc/X11/xinit/.Xresources sysmodmap=/etc/X11/xinit/.Xmodmap # merge in defaults and keymaps if [ -f $sysresources ]; then xrdb -merge $sysresources fi if [ -f $sysmodmap ]; then xmodmap $sysmodmap fi if [ -f "$userresources" ]; then xrdb -merge "$userresources" fi if [ -f "$usermodmap" ]; then xmodmap "$usermodmap" fi # start some nice programs if [ -d /etc/X11/xinit/xinitrc.d ] ; then for f in /etc/X11/xinit/xinitrc.d/?*.sh ; do [ -x "$f" ] && . "$f" done unset f fi #twm & #xclock -geometry 50x50-1+1 & #xterm -geometry 80x50+494+51 & #xterm -geometry 80x20+494-0 & #exec xterm -geometry 80x66+0+0 -name login exec i3Note: I already tried only using twm but it produced the same (or similiar?) crash as with i3I searched for conf files in /etc/X11/xorg.conf.d/ but there was only a 00-keyboard.conf file which I didn't delete.Next I searched in /usr/share/X11/xorg.conf.d and found several configuration files for radeon, amdgpu and a few others.
